## [v1.72.0] - 2026-06-19
### Added
- 6 new test cases from industry research (R192 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-139** [P1] CVE-2026-20700 iOS/iPadOS/macOS/tvOS/watchOS/visionOS dyld (dynamic linker) zero-day patched in iOS 26.3 (Feb 12 2026) — Apple's security advisory: "An attacker with memory write capability may be able to execute arbitrary code. Apple is aware of a report that this issue may have been exploited in an extremely sophisticated attack against specific targeted individuals on versions of iOS before iOS 26." Discovered by Google's Threat Analysis Group (TAG). The vulnerability lives in dyld — Apple's dynamic link editor — affecting EVERY iOS version since iPhone 1.0 (a 19-year-old bug, the longest-lived iOS vuln patched in 2026). Patched across iOS/iPadOS/macOS/tvOS/watchOS/visionOS 26.3. iOS-DYLD-LINKER-DECADE-OLD-EXPLOIT-CHAIN dimension distinct from B-110 (China NVDB iOS-WebKit RED ALERT — WebKit rendering layer) because CVE-2026-20700 is the OS-level dynamic-linker layer BELOW WebKit, requires memory-write precondition so it is an EXPLOIT-CHAIN final-stage component rather than a no-click zero-day; distinct from B-097 (iOS 26.5 generic 80+ vuln patch-list) because S-139 is a SPECIFIC in-the-wild-exploited decade-old dyld CVE patched 4 months earlier in iOS 26.3; distinct from S-041 (WebKit same-origin bypass CVE-2026-20643 — WebKit Navigation API) because S-041 is WebKit-layer and S-139 is OS-loader-layer. Affects GameZipper's ~20% iOS Safari traffic — pre-iOS-26.3 users are exploitable as the final stage of a multi-stage attack chain (WebKit memory-write via S-137 ANGLE bug → dyld code execution via S-139). (theregister.com/2026/02/12/apple_ios_263/ Feb 12 2026; blog.csdn.net/smellycat000/article/details/158033092 Feb 12 2026)
- **S-140** [P1] CVE-2026-3910 + CVE-2026-3909 Chrome V8 + Skia dual-0day pair (March 18 2026) — Google紧急修复Chrome浏览器中两个遭野外利用的0Day漏洞: CVE-2026-3910 (Chrome V8 JavaScript/WebAssembly engine sandbox-bypass → arbitrary code execution via crafted HTML) + CVE-2026-3909 (Chrome Skia 2D graphics library OOB WRITE via crafted HTML) — both ACTIVELY EXPLOITED IN THE WILD at time of patch. DUAL-0DAY-V8-AND-SKIA-PAIR-ACTIVELY-EXPLOITED dimension distinct from S-115 (Chrome 150 DevTools drawElementImage blank-canvas — a QA-TOOL bug not a security exploit) and S-088 (CVE-2026-5281 Dawn WebGPU UAF — a single WebGPU subsystem bug) because S-140 is a PAIRED exploit chain combining JS-engine sandbox-bypass (V8) with graphics-renderer memory corruption (Skia) — a malicious Monetag/AdSense creative could chain CVE-2026-3910 (escape V8 sandbox) + CVE-2026-3909 (corrupt Skia rendering buffer) to achieve full renderer compromise. David Shipley (Beauceron Security) warned "如果不管理浏览器补丁,遭受攻击的风险每天都在增加" (if you don't manage browser patches, attack risk grows daily). (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_87569ba00d309252 March 18 2026)
- **S-141** [P1] SANDWORM_MODE npm supply-chain worm (Feb 28 2026, QQ News / Socket research) — 19+ impersonation packages targeting popular dev tools + AI tools; multi-stage payload: (1) steal secrets from local environment + CI systems; (2) use stolen tokens to MODIFY OTHER REPOSITORIES (propagation via stolen write access); (3) NOVEL EVASION — "SANDWORM_*" environment-variable switches embedded in runtime control logic toggle which payload stage runs: absent in static-analysis scanner sandboxes (package looks benign) but present in production CI runners (full malicious payload activates). ENV-VARIABLE-TOGGLED-RUNTIME-EVASION dimension distinct from S-131 (Axios version-history-forgery — forges a clean version-history TRAIL to fool metadata-trusting scanners) and S-124 (Glassworm invisible-Unicode source-text-level obfuscation — hides malicious logic in invisible Unicode characters) because S-141 hides malicious logic behind an env-var CONDITIONAL so the source reads as a benign feature-flag toggle; distinct from S-107 (Red Hat Miasma worm — compromised-vendor-namespace propagation) because S-141 propagates via stolen DEVELOPER CREDENTIALS to modify other repos; distinct from S-135 (CanisterWorm — ICP decentralized-blockchain C2) because S-141 uses traditional token-theft propagation. Directly relevant to GameZipper's Hermes/Claude Code/MCP build pipeline which has broad tool access — env-var-conditional evasion specifically defeats Socket/Snyk/Dependabot static scanners that execute in isolated sandboxes WITHOUT production env vars. (new.qq.com/rain/a/20260228A047F100 Feb 28 2026)
- **C-114** [P2] Anthropic Mythos AI vuln-GENERATION model (April 8 2026 Anthropic statement; corroborated June 9 2026 Claude Fable 5 leak) — Anthropic publicly confirmed it developed an internal AI model named "Mythos" capable of generating zero-day exploits at scale, and decided NOT to release it because it would "以一种不好的方式破坏互联网" (break the internet in a bad way). Corroborated June 9 2026 by a leaked Claude Fable 5 system-prompt revealing the Claude 5 model family's tiered structure with a "Mythos-level" tier ABOVE Claude Opus. AI-VULN-GENERATION-CAPABILITY-MATURITY dimension distinct from S-113 (Anthropic Mythos 100 Chromium zero-days in 15 days — DEFENSIVE discovery that Anthropic disclosed to Chromium for patching) because C-114 confirms the OFFENSIVE counterpart — Anthropic acknowledged an internal Mythos variant can GENERATE exploit code; distinct from S-112 (Microsoft 33-package dependency-confusion — traditional supply-chain) because C-114 is AI-driven exploit generation not human-driven attack; distinct from C-113 (vibe-coding AI-generated code nondeterminism) because C-113 is unintentional AI-code risk while C-114 is intentional AI-exploit capability. Implication: a Mythos-class AI in the hands of a different vendor (or a future Anthropic policy change, or a weights leak — which the Claude Fable 5 system-prompt leak June 9 2026 shows IS possible) could generate working exploits for any GameZipper web-game feature within hours, compressing the CVE-disclosure-to-mass-exploitation window from 20h SLA (S-057) to minutes. (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_45769d629dd14252 April 8 2026; so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_2156a27d43031152 June 9 2026)
- **G-147** [P3] Android XR + Project Aura first consumer WebXR AR glasses shipping 2026 (Google I/O May 19 2026 + XREAL May 20 2026 + W3C WebXR AR Module Level 1 + Meta IWSDK May 12 2026) — Google announced Android XR at Google I/O 2026 attempting to "在XR时代复刻Android" (replicate Android in the XR era) after Apple Vision Pro failed to establish the category. XREAL immediately announced Project Aura (May 20 2026) as the world's first Android XR AR glasses, confirmed for global release in 2026. The W3C Immersive Web Working Group maintains WebXR Augmented Reality Module Level 1 (w3.org/TR/webxr-ar-module-1). Meta released an AI-upgraded Immersive Web SDK (IWSDK) May 12 2026 integrating AI-coding tools + agentic workflow, lowering the WebXR dev barrier so single-developer studios can ship WebXR modes. ANDROID-XR-WEBXR-AR-FORM-FACTOR dimension distinct from C-073 (foldable display viewport resize — 2D viewport) because G-147 is a 3D-immersive dimension change (entering/exiting AR session with passthrough camera, hand tracking, spatial anchors); distinct from P-029 (120Hz VRR rendering — refresh rate) because G-147 is rendering-pipeline (WebXR render loop differs from rAF); distinct from existing WebGPU dimensions because WebXR is the IMMERSIVE-SESSION API that wraps WebGPU/WebGL — complementary not overlapping. GameZipper game pages must not crash on XR UA strings or when `navigator.xr` is present; future AR-enhanced modes become viable once Android XR install base grows. (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_2256a1bb58622052 May 31 2026; so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_8946a0d520590152 May 20 2026; so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_0316a02db6174952 May 12 2026; w3.org/TR/webxr-ar-module-1)
- **W-173** [P2] Chrome MV3 migration typosquatting window — malicious MV3-compliant typosquatted clones capture abandoned MV2 user base (EditThisCookie???? 30K-50K user capture + June 16 2026 final kill switch) — Google's Chrome MV2→MV3 migration has a SIDE EFFECT beyond the kill date (W-151 covers June 30 2026 hard-kill): when legitimate MV2 extensions are delisted for non-MV3-compliance, malicious MV3-compliant typosquatted clones with near-identical names appear in Chrome Web Store and capture the abandoned user base. Canonical case: EditThisCookie (3M+ users) was delisted for MV2-non-compliance; malicious clone EditThisCookie???? (four trailing question-mark chars) was downloaded by 30K-50K users before Google took action; clone contains obfuscated code, links to fraud site, steals sensitive info (especially on Facebook), includes phishing + ad-distribution; clone was updated to MV3-compliance faster than original developer. MV3-MIGRATION-TYPOSQUATTING-WINDOW dimension distinct from W-151 (Manifest V2 final hard kill Chrome 150/151 June 30 2026 — the kill DATE) because W-173 is the SIDE EFFECT — typosquatting attack-window created when legitimate extensions disappear; distinct from S-110 (typosquatted npm packages — NPM registry) because W-173 covers the CHROME WEB STORE (end-user browser extensions); distinct from S-128 (OpenClaw ClawHub AI-agent-marketplace) because W-173 covers the Chrome browser extension store; distinct from W-135 (MV3 ad-blocker disruption declarativeNetRequest limitations — functional degradation) because W-173 is SECURITY degradation — malicious clones exploiting the migration. GameZipper players using ad-blockers/cookie-editors who search for replacements after June 30 2026 will encounter malicious typosquatted clones as top results. (163.com/dy/article/JKVEM9CF0511BLFD.html Jan 3 2025 EditThisCookie???? case; new.qq.com/rain/a/20260616A09EJK00 June 16 2026 final kill switch)

- **B-110** [P1] China NVDB (工信部 国家网络安全威胁和漏洞信息共享平台) iOS-WebKit RED ALERT (红色预警, April 3 2026) — foreign-APT in-the-wild exploitation of iOS WebKit confirmed across 42,000+ compromised iPhones in CN; single malicious webpage → no-interaction RCE → full device control; covers CVE-2025-43529 + CVE-2025-14174 (both Google TAG discovered, both in-the-wild exploited); SOVEREIGN-CERT-IOS-WEBKIT-RED-ALERT dimension distinct from W-167 (CN Shai-Hulud npm advisory — npm-specific) and B-097 (iOS 26.5 generic patch-list) because B-110 is iOS-WebKit-specific, RED-ALERT-level (highest), and confirmed across 42K+ devices; directly relevant to GameZipper's ~20% iOS Safari traffic — a malicious Monetag/AdSense creative delivered to an unpatched iOS Safari player achieves the same no-interaction RCE (blog.csdn.net/xixixi7777/article/details/160202543 June 11 2026; new.qq.com/rain/a/20260119A01E5F00 Jan 19 2026; new.qq.com/rain/a/20251229A06B2H00 Dec 29 2025)
- **S-137** [P1] CVE-2025-14174 / CVE-2025-43529 Cross-Vendor ANGLE Memory-OOB shared CVE (Apple Jan 19 2026; Google Threat Analysis Group discovered; both in-the-wild exploited) — CVE-2025-14174 is an ANGLE memory-OOB that affects BOTH iOS Safari/WebKit (via ANGLE Metal backend per trac.webkit.org/wiki/AngleforWebGL) AND Chrome/Chromium (via ANGLE DirectX/Vulkan backend) — the CROSS-VENDOR-ANGLE-SHARED-CVE dimension: a single graphics-library-layer CVE propagates to multiple browser vendors simultaneously, so a patched-Chrome-but-unpatched-iOS (or vice versa) means the SAME exploit creative can hit whichever platform lags; distinct from S-088 (CVE-2026-5281 Dawn WebGPU UAF — Chrome-Dawn-specific) and B-087 (iOS 26 WebKit WebGPU memory-limits regression — API-bug) because S-137 is the SHARED-LIBRARY-LAYER dimension (cnblogs.com/clnchanpin/p/19475745 Jan 13 2026; support.apple.com/en-us/125884; new.qq.com/rain/a/20260119A01E5F00 Jan 19 2026)
- **W-172** [P2] Safari 26 stable ship + last-minute privacy-feature PULLBACK (cloud.tencent.com June 19 2026) — WebKit bug 134226694 (auto-strip gclid/fbclid tracking params in regular browsing mode) + WebKit bug 134227067 (prevent fingerprinting for known tracking scripts) were BOTH beta-announced for Safari 26 but REMOVED from the final Safari 26 stable release — gclid/fbclid tracking is NOT blocked in shipped Safari 26; SAFARI-ANNOUNCED-PRIVACY-FEATURE-PULLED-LAST-MINUTE dimension distinct from S-081 (Safari 27 deliberate deprecations) and B-090 (Safari 27 WWDC26 525 fixes) because W-172 is the BETA-TO-STABLE-PULLBACK pattern — affects GameZipper Monetag/AdSense attribution (gclid/fbclid still work in Safari 26 stable, contradicting beta announcement) AND generalizes: any Safari beta feature is at-risk-of-pullback before stable ship; QA plans based on WWDC26 announcements (B-108/B-090) should be conditional on stable-ship confirmation in September 2026 (cloud.tencent.com/developer/article/2637644 June 19 2026)
- **S-138** [P2] Safari 26.5 WebRTC process-crash fix (Apple May 14 2026) — Safari 26.5 security list includes a fix for a WebRTC bug that could cause the Safari browser process to abnormally crash affecting audio/video communication scenarios; also fixed CVE-2026-28962 (CSP bypass → sensitive-info disclosure — already covered by S-040 v1.19.0) and multiple memory-corruption crash issues; SAFARI-26.5-WEBRTC-CRASH-FIX dimension distinct from S-085 (CVE-2026-9111 WebRTC UAF RCE — Linux Chromium) and B-086 (Firefox 151 MFSA2026-46 sandbox-escape batch) because S-138 is Safari-specific WebRTC crash (DoS / process-termination) from a different bug class; any future GameZipper game using WebRTC (peer-to-peer multiplayer, voice chat) on Safari 26/26.4 (pre-fix) could crash mid-session (developer.apple.com/news May 14 2026 Safari 26.5 release notes; so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_0236a054d4370952 May 14 2026)
- **A-040** [P2] PHY041/phy-a11y-reviewer automated WCAG 2.2 AA web-application reviewer toolchain (GitHub March 6 2026; corroborated by a11ycheck mrgig.com May 16 2026) — a category of tools that takes either a URL or codebase and produces a structured WCAG 2.2 AA conformance report (87 criteria including the 9 new 2.2 criteria per A-027), going beyond what axe-core/WAVE catch (30-40% per A-031); AUTOMATED-WCAG-2.2-AA-REVIEWER-TOOLCHAIN dimension distinct from A-034 (US ADA Title II — legal/regulatory), A-037 (iOS 27 Accessibility framework rewrite — Apple-API-specific), and A-038/A-039 (lawsuit statistics) because A-040 is the TOOLING-AUTOMATION dimension — actionable integration of an open-source reviewer into the GameZipper pre-commit/CI pipeline (matching the existing gz-pre-commit + sync-game-counts.sh pattern in the post-deploy-verification skill) to catch WCAG 2.2 AA regressions before they ship across 280+ game pages + tools subdomain (github.com/PHY041/phy-a11y-reviewer March 6 2026; mrgig.com May 16 2026; blog.csdn.net/gitblog_00365/article/details/155290334 April 20 2026)
- **P-069** [P2] WebGPU 39× draw-call throughput + 2.75× texture-sampling rate vs WebGL2 — concrete migration-decision numbers (CSDN AWS WebGPU实战 Three.js March 24 2026; corroborated by zhihu WebGPU performance analysis Aug 2 2022) — WebGL 2.0 caps at ~12,000 draw calls/frame before CPU-bottlenecked stalls; WebGPU sustains ~470,000 draw calls/frame = 39× throughput; texture sampling 8 GB/s (WebGL2) vs 22 GB/s (WebGPU) = 2.75×; render perf 3×+ WebGL; compute perf 50×+ WebGL (measured on M1 Pro + RTX 2060 Super); CONCRETE-WebGPU-PERF-NUMBERS-FOR-MIGRATION-CASE dimension distinct from P-030 (WebGPU 70% coverage + coarse 15× compute) and P-047 (WebGPU 8.5× draw calls — real-game sustained workload, different metric) because P-069 provides FOUR specific ceiling numbers each tied to a game-workload profile (draw-call-heavy / texture-heavy / render-heavy / compute-heavy) — sets the migration-decision threshold for any future high-sprite-count game (bullet-hell, particle-heavy match-3, large-tile puzzle) that would cap at the WebGL2 12K-draw-call ceiling (blog.csdn.net/awscloud/article/details/146470071 March 24 2026; zhuanlan.zhihu.com/p/387054998 Aug 2 2022)

- **W-170** [P2] 2026 cybersecurity report: AI rewrites threat landscape — AI-Agent身份冒充 (AI-Agent identity impersonation) + API规模化攻击 (API-scale attacks via AI-driven endpoint enumeration) + AI浏览器/AI手机"黑箱"风险 (AI-browser/AI-phone blackbox risk — non-auditable AI-mediated decisions); IDC predicts 70% of organizations adopt composite AI by 2026; thesis: cybersecurity moves from "边界防护 (perimeter defense)" to "信任重构 (trust reconstruction)" — the user ↔ AI ↔ application trust chain replaces the network perimeter as the locus of defense; NEW-AI-DRIVEN-ATTACK-DIMENSION vector distinct from S-101 (AI-assistant prompt injection — single technique) and S-127 (cryptojacking recommendation — single incident) because W-170 is the THREAT-LANDSCAPE-LEVEL shift the GameZipper threat model must accommodate as a whole; distinct from W-164 (ChatGPT sponsored content — economic issue) because W-170 is a security-and-trust issue; affects GameZipper's agent-based build pipeline (Hermes/Claude Code/MCP per S-128/S-130/S-133), BI dashboard API surface, and AI-browser-engagement-metric attribution (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_08069cbb35774752 March 31 2026; new.qq.com/rain/a/20251224A02X1V00 Dec 24 2025)
- **W-171** [P2] AOSP source-code publication cadence change effective 2026 — Google announced (effective 2026) that to align with the "trunk stable" development model and ensure ecosystem platform stability, Google will publish Android source code to AOSP in Q2 and Q4 only (not continuously); `android-latest-release` manifest branch always references most recent release pushed to AOSP; ANDROID-OS-DEVELOPMENT-CADENCE dimension distinct from B-107 (Android 17 memory-pressure enforcement — platform BEHAVIOR) because W-171 is a DEVELOPMENT-CADENCE change governing when Android source (including security patches) becomes available for OEM firmware incorporation → determines when patches reach end-user Android Chrome WebView that runs GameZipper mobile games; distinct from B-099 (Android June 2026 Security Bulletin — single patch batch) because W-171 is the CADENCE that governs when patches get into AOSP and therefore OEM firmware; affects ~70% Android mobile traffic — patch-to-device time may grow from ~30 days to ~120-180 days; new web-platform features (CSS Gap Decorations, WebGPU, bfcache WebSocket) reach Android Chrome in batches aligned with AOSP drops rather than continuously, lagging desktop Chrome by months (source.android.google.cn/security/bulletin/chromecast Dec 9 2025; source.android.google.cn/security/bulletin)
- **S-136** [P1] CVE-2026-21385 Qualcomm Android Graphics OOB-read CVSS 7.8 (in-the-wild exploited, Google March 2026 Android Security Bulletin) — Qualcomm Graphics component buffer over-read via integer-overflow when adding user-supplied data → memory corruption; Google Android security team reported to Qualcomm Dec 18 2025; Qualcomm notified customers Feb 2 2026; Google's March 2026 bulletin explicitly stated "indications that CVE-2026-21385 may be under limited, targeted exploitation" — ACTIVELY EXPLOITED; March 2026 Android update patched 129 total vulns including CRITICAL CVE-2026-0006 (System-component RCE, no privileges/interaction required); ANDROID-GPU-DRIVER-CVE-IN-THE-WILD dimension distinct from B-099 (June bulletin — generic batch) because S-136 is a SPECIFIC in-the-wild GPU-driver CVE affecting Android Chrome WebView graphics stack; distinct from S-088 (CVE-2026-5281 Dawn WebGPU UAF — Chrome-side) because S-136 is Qualcomm Adreno DRIVER-side, patched via Android system update (much slower than Chrome update) and per W-171 even slower under new AOSP Q2+Q4 cadence; affects Qualcomm/Adreno-majority Android traffic; GPU-driver exploit surface means a malicious WebGL/Canvas context (ad creative) could deliver the exploit (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_10069a7b0f989452 March 4 2026)
- **C-113** [P2] Vibe-coding methodology risk — Karpathy Feb 2 2025 tweet coinage "vibe coding" (writing code by accepting AI-suggested completions without rigorous review, trusting the AI's "vibe") became Collins English Dictionary 2025 Word of the Year; April 2026 云涌AI/钛媒体 published a 25000-character "History of the AI Programming Movement 2020-2026" retrospective positioning vibe coding as the dominant 2025-2026 software-development methodology; AI-GENERATED-CODE-NONDETERMINISM-QA-BYPASS dimension distinct from C-110 (DevTools CVE scanner — tool-as-vector) and C-111 (Purple-team LLM vuln scanning — defensive tooling) because C-113 is the METHODOLOGY dimension — the cultural practice of vibe coding that GameZipper's own pipeline operators (Claude Code subagents, Hermes orchestrators, puzzle-pipeline game generators) increasingly embody; AI-generated code is NONDETERMINISTIC (same prompt → different code per run), so deterministic QA systematically MISSES bugs that the AI introduced on THIS run but not LAST run; the post-deploy-verification skill documents MANY recurring bugs that are EXACTLY the vibe-coding failure mode (rAF cancelAnimationFrame template error in 55 games, splash-screen dead-lock in 5+ games, missing input handlers, BGM setInterval leaks, games-data.js orphan entries recurring 5+ times) — static scans "✅ PASS" then browser-test "❌ FAIL" is the canonical vibe-coding-QA-bypass (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_04569e9fe0604952 April 23 2026; Collins English Dictionary 2025 Word of the Year; Karpathy Feb 2 2025 tweet)

- **W-167** [P2] China 国家网络与信息安全信息通报中心 (National Cybersecurity Information Notification Center) official Shai-Hulud npm supply-chain advisory (May 26 2026) — China's national CERT-equivalent issued a formal public advisory confirming the npm "Shai-Hulud" (沙虫) supply-chain poisoning attack: 600+ malicious versions across 300+ packages affecting echarts-for-react, the entire @antv series, TanStack 42 packages, Mistral AI PyPI, timeago.js; the advisory provides a specific check-list including Claude Code hooks + VS Code tasks.json persistence (router_runtime.js, setup.mjs) — confirming S-130's AI-AGENT-CONFIG-FILE-PERSISTENCE vector is now national-CERT-recognized; SOVEREIGN-CERT-NPM-ADVISORY dimension distinct from S-130 (TanStack technical analysis — vendor/researcher writeup) and C-108 (npm worm methodology — framework) because W-167 is a NATIONAL-CERT-LEVEL ADVISORY confirming CN-jurisdiction operators have compliance obligations beyond vendor advisories (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_4186a15535e00252 May 26 2026)
- **C-111** [P2] Purple-team LLM vulnerability scanning methodology — PurPaaS / OWASP Agentic AI Top 10 / CSA Red teaming (github.com/topics/ai-vulnerability-assessment June 2 2026) — a category of open-source security-testing tools for automated red/blue-team (purple-team) assessment of locally-deployed LLMs via Ollama, scanning for prompt injection, model inversion, data leakage, jailbreaks, and adversarial abuse; PURPLE-TEAM-LLM-VULN-SCANNING dimension distinct from C-110 (DevTools CVE scanner — a tool that itself becomes a vector) and S-101 (AI-assistant browser extension prompt injection — an attack on a deployed AI) because C-111 is the DEFENSIVE-QA-TOOLING dimension — a category of testing tools GameZipper could adopt to PROACTIVELY test any AI feature it ships (AI hint systems, procedural-level generators, content moderation) AND to test the agent harness itself (Hermes/Claude Code per S-128 OpenClaw ClawHub + S-130 TanStack Shai-Hulud which targeted exactly this surface) (github.com/topics/ai-vulnerability-assessment June 2 2026)
- **C-112** [P2] Desktop-consumer-software supply-chain vector — DAEMON Tools disk-mount 2025 attack (Kaspersky March 27 2026 "The most notable supply-chain attacks of 2025" retrospective) — Kaspersky documents a targeted supply-chain attack delivered via DAEMON Tools (popular disk-image-mounting utility) compromising the update/distribution channel; DESKTOP-CONSUMER-SOFTWARE-SUPPLY-CHAIN dimension distinct from C-109 (Apifox desktop-client CDN poisoning — a DEVELOPER TOOL) and C-108 (npm worm methodology — a PACKAGE REGISTRY) because C-112 covers GENERAL consumer desktop software (Daemon Tools, WinRAR, 7-Zip, Notepad++) — a less-tracked vector because security teams focus on dev tools and package registries, but consumer desktop software is installed on every QA engineer's machine and often has auto-update with elevated privileges; a compromised DAEMON Tools updater on a QA workstation can pivot to compromising the GameZipper build environment via stolen creds, modified game files, or backdoored build scripts (kaspersky.com/blog/tag/supply-chain-attack/ March 27 2026)
- **P-068** [P2] WebGPU streaming buffers for progressive 3D-asset loading (PlayCanvas SuperSplat June 3 2026 news "New in SuperSplat: WebGPU and Streaming Bring Huge Performance Wins") — PlayCanvas announced SuperSplat achieves significant performance gains by combining WebGPU rendering with streaming buffer architecture: large 3D assets (Gaussian-splat point clouds, generalizes to large glTF models and textures) load progressively via WebGPU mapped buffers rather than monolithically, allowing first-paint before the full asset is in GPU memory; WEBGPU-STREAMING-BUFFERS-PROGRESSIVE-LOAD dimension distinct from P-027 (Chrome 148 native lazy-loading audio/video — different API) and P-067 (WASM-WebGPU shared-memory boundary — tests the BOUNDARY not the LOADING pattern) because P-068 tests the progressive large-asset loading pattern: first-paint time vs total-asset-size + GPU memory pressure during progressive mapping + the map/unmap synchronization window (playcanvas.com June 3 2026)

- **S-135** [P1] CanisterWorm / Namastex Labs AI-agent-company-targeted npm worm with ICP decentralized-blockchain C2 exfil endpoint (Socket + StepSecurity disclosure April 24 2026) — self-propagating CanisterWorm-class malware hit multiple npm packages tied to Namastex Labs (an agentic-AI company); exfils tokens/creds/API keys/SSH keys + cloud/CI/CD/K8s/Docker/LLM-platform config via TWO channels: a webhook AND an Internet Computer Protocol canister container endpoint (hardcoded ID cjn37-uyaaa-aaaac-qgnva-cai); TeamPCP/LiteLLM .pth-injection lineage; AI-AGENT-COMPANY SUPPLY-CHAIN + DECENTRALIZED-BLOCKCHAIN-C2 dimension distinct from S-130 TanStack TeamPCP because CanisterWorm (a) specifically profiles AI-agent vendors (aggregated AI keys), (b) exfils via an ICP canister that has no single registrar/hosting/jurisdiction to takedown — first documented use of a blockchain canister as npm-malware exfil endpoint, defeating traditional domain/IP egress blocking (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_85669eb09b517552 April 24 2026)
- **W-162** [P1] CVE-2026-32746 GNU InetUtils Telnetd LINEMODE SLC OOB-write CVSS 9.8 unauthenticated RCE (Israeli firm Dream March 11 2026; affects all telnetd versions ≤ 2.7) — LEGACY-DAEMON PROTOCOL-PARSER OVERFLOW dimension; distinct from S-086 NGINX/S-069 HTTP/2 (modern high-traffic services) because W-162 covers legacy text-protocol daemons (telnet/FTP/SMTP/SNMP) that linger on internal/build/embedded hosts; pattern generalizes to any server-side daemon with a legacy text-protocol parser being a CVSS-9.x unauth-RCE candidate (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_20169ba7a7d29552 March 18 2026)
- **W-163** [P1] CVE-2026-21992 Oracle Identity Manager / Web Services Manager unauthenticated HTTP RCE CVSS 9.8 (Oracle April 2026 CPU, disclosed March 23 2026; affects OIM 12.2.1.4.0 + 14.1.2.1.0 + OWSM same versions) — IDENTITY-INFRASTRUCTURE UNAUTH-RCE dimension; compromising the identity layer yields not one server but the ability to forge/mint credentials for every downstream federated/SSO/OAuth service that trusts it (force-multiplied compromise); distinct from S-037 SalesLoft OAuth-token-theft (SaaS vendor) because W-163 is direct RCE in the on-prem identity appliance; dimension applies to whatever auth provider GameZipper tooling trusts (Cloudflare Access, GitHub OAuth, customer-federated IdP) (so.html5.qq.com/page/real/search_news?docid=70000021_05869c1125c24352 March 23 2026)
- **W-164** [P2] ChatGPT 2026 sponsored-content / AI-advertising (The Information Dec 25 2025) — OpenAI employees prototyping sponsored/paid-result injection into ChatGPT answers ("2026 is likely the first year humans need an ad-blocker for AI"); AI-CHATBOT OFFICIAL-SPONSORED-CONTENT DISCOVERY-DISPLACEMENT dimension distinct from S-120 ChatGPhish/S-127 cryptojacking because the displacement is BY THE VENDOR (not an attacker) — when a player asks an AI "fun puzzle game?" a competitor's sponsored result displaces GameZipper's organic ranking with no recourse (cannot optimize for a sponsored slot you didn't buy); AI-era analogue of SEO-displacement with no optimization path; distinct from W-157 (unintentional error rate) because W-164 is intentional paid displacement (new.qq.com/rain/a/20251225A03OTE00 Dec 25 2025 — The Information via QQ News)
- **P-067** [P2] WebGPU + WASM shared-memory architecture 2026 — the 2026 browser-game perf pattern runs CPU-intensive workloads (physics/AI-ML/procedural/audio DSP) in WASM and GPU workloads in WebGPU, coordinating via SHARED MEMORY (WASM linear memory ↔ WebGPU mapped buffer) rather than copy-based marshalling; WASM-WebGPU SHARED-MEMORY BOUNDARY dimension distinct from P-045/P-047/P-060/P-062 (WebGPU in isolation) because P-067 tests the BOUNDARY where (a) WASM heap corruption silently corrupts a GPU-mapped buffer (no WASM error, GPU renders garbage), (b) WebGPU device-lost invalidates a buffer WASM still writes (WASM use-after-free), (c) layout mismatch (WASM float32 vs GPU packed-uint16-norm) produces corruption that looks like a render bug but is a memory-layout contract violation; failure mode (silent corruption, clean console) is exactly what post-deploy-verification's console-error check MISSES; relevant for any GameZipper game pairing WASM-compiled physics/ML with WebGPU rendering (tool.lu/article/7yi/detail June 3 2026; blog.csdn.net/gitblog_00372/article/details/158277179 March 4 2026; blog.csdn.net/gitblog_01177/article/details/158278649 March 27 2026)
- **C-110** [P2] Browser-DevTools-console CVE-scanner tool pattern (cloud.tencent.com/developer/article/2609303 June 18 2026 "GitHub CVE扫描器 一键发现React与Next.js安全漏洞") — "security tools" distributed as JS that the user pastes into the DevTools Console on a sensitive authenticated origin (github.com, cloud console, admin); the console inherits FULL page-origin privileges so a pasted script can read session cookies / make authenticated API calls / exfiltrate a PAT the user pasted "for scanning"; DEVTOOLS-CONSOLE-RUNNING-UNTRUSTED-JS dimension is self-XSS-by-consent camouflaged as CVE scanning (references real CVE-2025-55182 React2Shell + withdrawn CVE-2025-66478); distinct from S-123 (clipboard/Win+R OS-shell) because C-110 targets the BROWSER origin; distinct from S-029 (ad-iframe sandbox) because C-110 is code the DEVELOPER voluntarily pastes which no iframe sandbox blocks; GameZipper QA/operators routinely use consoles on sensitive origins (BI dashboard, Cloudflare, GitHub, production admin) — a "paste this CVE scanner" in a QA community could exfiltrate GitHub PAT / Cloudflare token / BI session; acute risk now that S-133 coverage means real CVE-scanner tools circulate mixed with malicious ones

## [v1.67.0] - 2026-06-18
### Added
- 8 new test cases from industry research (R187 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-130** [P0] TanStack/Mistral AI "Mini Shai-Hulud" TeamPCP cross-registry npm+PyPI supply-chain attack (May 11 2026, 62 packages/404 malicious versions, @tanstack/react-router 12M+ weekly downloads alone) — introduces four dimensions not seen in any prior S-104~S-129 npm case: (1) AI-AGENT-CONFIG-FILE-PERSISTENCE — payload persists in `.claude/settings.json`, `.vscode/tasks.json`, Kiro/MCP OAuth tokens (NOT in node_modules), so `npm uninstall` does NOT clean it; for GameZipper which runs Hermes subagents + Claude Code + MCP servers, a single compromised dependency persists across every subsequent agent invocation; (2) DEAD-MAN'S-SWITCH-WIPE-DAEMON — if operator revokes tokens BEFORE isolating the host, daemon wipes entire home directory as anti-forensics (defeats the standard "revoke first, isolate second" playbook); (3) GITHUB-ACTIONS-OIDC-TRUST-CHAIN BYPASS — fork `TanStack/router` as `zblgg/configuration`, PR triggers `pull_request_target` workflow with maintainer secrets in scope, drives OIDC-publish workflow to push to npm with cryptographically valid SLSA Level 3 signatures (defeats S-114 provenance trust signal); (4) PROC-MEM CREDENTIAL EXTRACTION on Linux runners reads `/proc/<pid>/mem` to extract even MASKED secrets; first TeamPCP campaign to harvest password managers (1Password, Bitwarden) alongside cloud creds (blog.csdn.net/weixin_42376192/article/details/161035915 May 11 2026; blog.csdn.net/weixin_47053301/article/details/161039802 May 13 2026; so.html5.qq.com May 14 2026 OpenAI response; github.com/Cobenian/shai-hulud-detect — 3,290+ confirmed bad versions)
- **S-131** [P1] Axios npm version-history-forgery supply-chain attack (March 31 2026; axios 300M+ weekly downloads; malicious `axios@1.14.1` + `axios@0.30.4`; cross-platform RAT — macOS Mach-O, Linux Python `/tmp/ld.py`; C2 `sfrclak.com:8000` / IP `142.11.206.73`) — the VERSION-HISTORY-FORGERY technique is the novel dimension: attacker published a CLEAN `plain-crypto-js@4.2.0` first to forge a benign version-history trail, then 39 min later dropped malicious `plain-crypto-js@4.2.1` + the backdoored axios versions, so automated review tools that diff `new_version` vs `previous_version` see only a small "routine bump" diff against the clean predecessor, NOT the full payload; distinct from S-126 (eslint-config-prettier maintainer-phishing) because NO human was phished — the attacker forged a clean version-history trail that automated review tools trust; GameZipper angle: a subagent that "reviews version history" before installing axios (the recommended S-126 mitigation) is FOOLED because the history looks clean (download.csdn.net/blog/column/11568299/159802674 April 2026 weekly report; StepSecurity / FreeBuf March 31 2026)
- **S-132** [P1] Langflow CVE-2026-33017 (CVSS 9.3, exploited in the wild 20 hours after disclosure) — AI-low-code-workflow-platform exec() RCE; `POST /api/v1/build_public_tmp/{flow_id}/flow` runs Python `exec()` on attacker-controlled `data` parameter with NO auth and NO sandbox; CISA KEV added, fix-by April 8 2026; affects Langflow ≤ 1.8.1, fixed in 1.9.0.dev8; AI-WORKFLOW-PLATFORM-EXEC-RCE dimension distinct from S-119 (Marimo LLM-agent post-exploitation — Langflow is the PLATFORM-LEVEL exec() not post-compromise agent tool use); distinct from CVE-2025-3248 CVSS 9.8 (targeted `/api/v1/validate/code`) — same root cause reused via a DIFFERENT endpoint, confirming the pattern that once a platform has an exec()-on-untrusted-input design flaw, additional endpoints exposing the same call surface keep appearing; 20-hour weaponization window confirms S-113 (Mythos) + C-102 (AI-discovered-CVE cadence); GameZipper relevance: if GameZipper ever embeds an LLM-agent/workflow platform (Langflow, Flowise, n8n, Dify), the exec()-on-untrusted-input surface becomes a P0 unauthenticated RCE vector (blog.csdn.net/qq_37865996/article/details/159549218 March 27 2026; blog.csdn.net/2302_79436907/article/details/159896254 June 10 2026; so.html5.qq.com March 23 2026; blog.csdn.net/weixin_45635831/article/details/159563953 March 28 2026)
- **C-109** [P1] Apifox desktop-client CDN poisoning (April 2026 weekly security report) — API-testing tool Apifox had its CDN update channel compromised for 18 days, every download during the window shipped a credential-stealing payload exfiltrating SSH private keys + Kubernetes service-account tokens; DESKTOP-DEV-TOOL-CDN-POISONING dimension distinct from EVERY npm-registry case (S-104 ~ S-131) because npm attacks poison a specific version the developer explicitly installs (developer can pin a known-good version to avoid); CDN poisoning poisons the DELIVERY CHANNEL ITSELF — every download is compromised regardless of which version the user selects, so the "pin to a safe version" mitigation (S-126, S-131) is completely ineffective; distinct from S-070 (web game supply-chain CDN tampering) which covers GAME ASSETS not DEVELOPER TOOLS; GameZipper relevance: Hermes CLI, Claude Code, kachilu-browser all have auto-update — a poisoned update channel makes the tool a persistent backdoor inside the build environment, every game built during the window is suspect (download.csdn.net/blog/column/11568299/159802674 April 2026 weekly security report)
- **B-105** [P1] TA446 (Russian-nexus APT) first in-the-wild iOS/iCloud exploit-kit deployment codenamed "DarkSword" (April 2026 weekly security report) — prior to April 2026, iOS exploit kits were nation-state-developed, used against a handful of high-value targets, NEVER deployed by profit-driven APT groups against the general population; TA446's DarkSword deployment marks the transition of iOS exploit kits from state-only to APT-criminal deployment, meaning the mobile-Safari WebKit attack surface (every casual-game iOS player) is now a real in-the-wild target; iOS-APT-IN-THE-WILD dimension distinct from B-087 (iOS 26 WebKit regression — a BUG) and B-097 (iOS 26.5 80+ vuln advisory — Apple's BUG disclosure) because B-105 documents an OFFENSIVE KIT ACTIVELY DEPLOYED against iOS users — "hole in the fence" (bug) vs "thief walking through the hole" (APT deployment); distinct from S-052 (single Safari 26.5 CVE) because B-105 is a deployed multi-exploit kit (likely chains several CVEs, some 0-day at deployment); GameZipper relevance: a DarkSword-style kit chaining a WebKit 0-day via crafted canvas/WebGL context could be delivered through a malicious Monetag/AdSense ad creative (per S-118 DoubleClick/DesckVB) to GameZipper iOS players (download.csdn.net/blog/column/11568299/159802674 April 2026 weekly security report)
- **W-159** [P2] Rolldown 1.0 + Vite 8 build-toolchain migration (Rolldown RC Jan 21 2026, Vite 8 Beta Dec 4 2025, stable release June 2026 per JS Weekly Week 20) — Rust-written Rolldown replaces BOTH Rollup (production) AND esbuild (dev) in Vite 8; 10-30x faster than Rollup; CONFIG-API SHAPE CHANGE: `build.rollupOptions` → `build.rolldownOptions`, `esbuild` config option → `oxc` option; BUILD-TOOLCHAIN-MIGRATION dimension distinct from B-103 (Basemark URL migration — TOOL-URL change) because W-159 is a CONFIG-API SHAPE change — a build config that worked on Vite 7 silently uses default values on Vite 8 because `rollupOptions` is ignored (new key `rolldownOptions`), producing a DIFFERENT bundle without any error; distinct from G-137 (game-rendering tech choice) because W-159 covers BUILD-TOOL choice (affects bundle shape, CDN cache keys, subresource-integrity hashes); GameZipper relevance: games are mostly single-file HTML+JS (not Vite-built), but any Vite-built npm library imported into a game changes bundle shape when upstream migrates, breaking subresource-integrity hashes and CDN cache keys silently (antfu/skills rolldown-migration.md May 28 2026; blog.csdn.net/xfy196/article/details/157909765 April 15 2026; cloud.tencent.com/developer/article/2679559 JS Weekly Week 20; VoidZero / Evan You Vite 8 Beta Dec 4 2025)
- **W-160** [P2] ShinyHunters breach of the European Commission's AWS cloud infrastructure (April 2026 weekly security report) — threat actor ShinyHunters exfiltrated 350GB of data from the EU Commission's AWS environment, demonstrating that even a major government institution with dedicated security teams can have its cloud infrastructure comprehensively compromised; GOVERNMENT-CLOUD-BREACH-PUBLIC-SECTOR-RISK dimension distinct from A-034/A-035 (ADA Title II COMPLIANCE deadlines) because W-160 covers ACTIVE COMPROMISE — a GameZipper customer in .gov/.edu (library, school district, municipality) can have their Cloudflare/CDN credentials exfiltrated via a breached upstream provider, and GameZipper content served THROUGH that customer's proxy/CDN becomes a vector or casualty; distinct from S-052/S-118 (technical exploits) because W-160 is a SUPPLY-CHAIN-TRUST dimension — "are GameZipper's UPSTREAM PROVIDERS (Cloudflare, GitHub Pages, AWS for BI dashboard, Monetag/AdSense) secure, and what happens when one is breached?"; GameZipper relevance: public-sector customers' own cloud infra is a target; a breach of their infra can pivot to compromising the GameZipper content they serve to their users (download.csdn.net/blog/column/11568299/159802674 April 2026 weekly security report)
- **W-161** [P2] Suno/Udio AI-music copyright litigation (filed June 24 2024 by UMG + Warner + Sony against Suno AI and Udio, ongoing through 2026) — first major AI-GENERATED-AUDIO copyright litigation; outcome will determine whether AI-generated music is derivative work (infringing) or transformative fair use (non-infringing); AI-GENERATED-AUDIO COPYRIGHT LITIGATION dimension distinct from W-146 (FTC Honda dark-pattern — consumer-protection) because W-161 is INTELLECTUAL-PROPERTY (who owns AI-trained output); distinct from S-127 (AI chatbot cryptojacking — security) because W-161 is a LEGAL vector; GameZipper relevance: per `mlops/models/audiocraft-audio-generation` and `creative/songwriting-and-ai-music` (Suno) skills, AI-generated audio is a documented GameZipper tooling path; if a GameZipper game ships BGM generated by Suno/Udio and the litigation concludes AI music IS derivative infringement, every shipped AI track becomes retroactively infringing, rightsholders can DMCA takedown game pages, GameZipper may face secondary-infringement claims; even with vendor indemnification, liability cap may be far below actual damages (toutiao.com/topic/7484078372046407732/ 2026; toutiao.com/topic/7488894961577035812/ 2026; huanqiu.com via toutiao 2026; sourceforge.net/software/ai-music-generators 2026 — Suno commercial-use ToS)

## [v1.66.0] - 2026-06-17
### Added
- 8 new test cases from industry research (R186 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-128** [P1] OpenClaw ClawHub — AI-AGENT-MARKETPLACE supply-chain attack where the #1 most-installed skill on OpenClaw's marketplace was malware, executing inside every agent runtime that loaded it with full tool-call privileges (April 8 2026); AI-AGENT-SKILL-MARKETPLACE-AS-VECTOR dimension distinct from every prior npm/package case (S-104~S-127) because the vector is an AI agent's skill store, not a package registry — the malicious code runs INSIDE the agent's privileged tool-calling sandbox (terminal, file write, web fetch, git push) rather than at install-time; persistence is per-agent-session not per-install; directly relevant to GameZipper which runs Hermes skills + Kanban workers + Claude Code subagents with broad tool access; mitigation: skill provenance allowlist, source-code audit on install, network-egress allowlist during runs, canary-token skill (awesomeagents.ai/news/openclaw-clawhub-malware-supply-chain April 8 2026)
- **S-129** [P1] ClickFix macOS 26.4 Script Editor AppleScript-delivery variant — the ClickFix social-engineering family upgraded in April 2026 to bypass macOS 26.4 protections by abusing the built-in Script Editor (脚本编辑器) and osascript; the user pastes an AppleScript snippet that uses `do shell script` to fetch + execute the real payload, bypassing Gatekeeper + notarization + quarantine because Script Editor is Apple-signed and the user explicitly authorizes the run (so.html5.qq.com April 9 2026); macOS-APPLESCRIPT-EDITOR-DELIVERY dimension distinct from S-123 (Windows Win+R/PowerShell clipboard self-typed execution) — same creative, platform-specific payload; GameZipper Monetag/AdSense ad slots could serve the macOS variant to the ~17% Mac traffic that would never fall for a Win+R instruction; mitigation: ad-creative scanner extension for both Win+R AND osascript/Script-Editor indicators, iframe sandbox hardening denying clipboard-write, macOS ClickFix awareness in gamezipper-qa Pitfalls
- **C-107** [P2] Razer QA Companion-AI vision-based zero-integration bug detection + reproduction-step generation at GDC 2026 — Razer's QA Companion-AI watches the running game via screen capture, detects visual bugs (broken sprites, stuck animations, UI overlap, missing textures) using a vision model, and auto-generates bug reports with reproduction steps + screenshots + suggested priority (razer.com/blog GDC 2026; chinaz.com May 6 2026; so.html5.qq.com March 12 2026; weibo Razer Oct 30 2025; digitaltrends.com March 2025 AI QA Copilot predecessor); CONSUMER-PERIPHERAL-VENDOR-VISION-QA dimension distinct from C-093 (enterprise Capcom/EA agentic AI — requires API integration) and C-106 (Poki submission gate — platform-side) because Razer's tool is zero-integration (operates on screen capture, no code changes), making it retrofit-friendly for GameZipper's already-deployed pure-Canvas catalog where DOM/locator QA misses; mitigation: POC a vision-QA tool on 5 representative Canvas games, add vision-baseline diff to post-deploy-verification Phase 4, catalog GameZipper vision-bug taxonomy
- **C-108** [P2] npm supply-chain-worm 2026 methodology framework — comprehensive methodology documenting the full evolution of the 2025-2026 npm worm family from credential-theft-only → cloud-infrastructure-persistence → production-environment-compromise; unifies the discrete CVEs/attacks (S-104, S-105, S-106, S-107, S-111, S-114, S-116, S-121, S-125, S-126) into a single defensive framework rather than N disconnected point-fixes (blog.csdn.net/weixin_42376192/article/details/160780907 May 5 2026 CSDN shai-hulud; unit42.paloaltonetworks.com June 2026); META-METHODOLOGY-FRAMEWORK dimension — the key insight is that a defense catching only Stage 1 (credential theft) is defeated by an attacker who reached Stage 2 (cloud persistence via IAM/OAuth/CI runner backdoor) before Stage 1 was detected; GameZipper's existing defenses are all Stage-1; mitigation: add Stage-2 cloud-persistence audit (enumerate + scope + rotate long-lived creds) + Stage-3 production-tamper audit (weekly live-vs-HEAD byte hash diff)
- **B-104** [P2] ChromeOS 148 cert-configuration-system migration preparing for ChromeOS 150 LTS — ChromeOS 148 stable-channel release (May 26 2026) whose primary change is a certificate-configuration-system migration that changes how ChromeOS trusts root CAs, how enterprise policies push cert bundles, and how TLS is validated; a QA runner pinned to the old cert bundle breaks with NET::ERR_CERT_AUTHORITY_INVALID (so.html5.qq.com May 26 2026; Google enterprise release notes); ChromeOS-CERT-CONFIG-MIGRATION dimension distinct from W-138 (ChromeOS 148 LTS designation — calendar note) and B-083 (ChromeOS 150 LTC lag — compat note) because B-104 is a CONCRETE TECHNICAL REGRESSION; GameZipper relevance: if GameZipper ever targets the ChromeOS education market (~20% US K-12), cert-migration breaks TLS for any user behind a corporate/school proxy injecting its own CA; mitigation: HTTPS endpoint validation across cert bundles (Mozilla NSS, ChromeOS 147/148/150, Android 16, iOS 27), TLS-fingerprint monitor, client-diversity TLS testing
- **W-158** [P2] Chrome 148 AI-mode via address bar / new tab page — Chrome 148 (May 7 2026) added an AI agent directly accessible from the Omnibox and new tab page, so a player asks "what is this game?" WITHOUT leaving the page or opening a sidebar; the AI auto-ingests the current page content + answers inline (so.html5.qq.com May 7 2026); BROWSER-NATIVE-AI-MODE-ADDRESS-BAR dimension distinct from W-125 (Chrome/Edge AI sidebar — separate UI surface) and W-157 (AI chatbot summary error rate — external chatbot) because W-158 is the AI embedded in the browser chrome itself, inheriting "I typed here so this is authoritative" trust with no explicit open step; a compromised game page's content is auto-ingested the moment the player hits Cmd+T; mitigation: Chrome 148 AI-mode ingestion audit on 10 representative games, page-content poison-resistance test, structured-data feeding test, address-bar AI opt-out investigation, Chrome 148 rollout monitor
- **A-039** [P2] WCAGsafe 2025 ADA-lawsuit statistics — 8,667 total ADA lawsuits in 2025 (higher-aggregate methodology than A-038's 3,117 federal because WCAGsafe also counts state-court + class-action + demand-letter cases), 5,000+ targeted websites, with breakdown of top plaintiff states, serial plaintiffs, and settlement costs ($25K-$75K per suit) (wcagsafe.com/blog/ada-lawsuit-statistics 2026); HIGHER-AGGREGATE-METHODOLOGY + SERIAL-PLAINTIFF-INTELLIGENCE dimension distinct from A-038 (3,117 federal + HHS Section 504) because A-039 adds the actionable plaintiff-side intelligence — which firms file the most suits, which states are highest-risk venues (NY/FL/CA/TX/IL), which accessibility issues they target most; this tells GameZipper WHERE to prioritize WCAG investment; mitigation: state-prioritized WCAG audit (cross-reference GameZipper top-traffic states vs top-plaintiff states), serial-plaintiff firm monitor, settlement-cost-benefit model, WCAG 2.2 AA conformance report refresh, demand-letter response playbook
- **G-146** [P2] StudioKrew hybrid-casual dynamic-difficulty-adjustment (DDA) flow-state protection methodology — 2026 hybrid-casual retention methodology uses DDA not to make the game "fake easy" but to keep the player in a flow state: reduce frustration spikes for new players (lower early-game difficulty floor), increase challenge for highly-engaged (raise difficulty ceiling), adapt the curve per-player based on real-time signals (deaths, time-per-level, retry-count); concrete implementation patterns: signal-collection layer + DDA-decision layer + difficulty-injection layer + A/B-testable difficulty arms (studiokrew.com/blog/hybrid-casual-games-vs-traditional-mobile-games March 27 2026); DDA-FLOW-STATE-PROTECTION dimension distinct from G-111 (AI adaptive difficulty fairness/rubber-banding — the FAIRNESS question) and G-145 (hyper-casual 48h lapse economics — WHEN to re-engage, not how to prevent lapse) — G-146 covers lapse-PREVENTION via correctly-implemented invisible DDA; poorly-implemented DDA (visible rubber-banding) is worse than no DDA because players detect it and feel manipulated; GameZipper relevance: the puzzle catalog (water-sort, sand-sort, sliding-puzzle) ships a FIXED level order per the puzzle-level-generator skill; G-146 demands a per-player adaptive curve; mitigation: DDA signal-collection audit, fixed-curve churn-baseline measurement, DDA feasibility POC on water-sort, invisible-DDA anti-pattern audit, flow-state proxy metric, per-genre DDA calibration

## [v1.65.0] - 2026-06-17
### Added
- 8 new test cases from industry research (R185 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-124** [P1] Glassworm — invisible Unicode source-code malware hiding payloads in homoglyph/bidi-override characters invisible to human code review AND static scanners (March 2026 wave, 150+ GitHub repos + npm + VS Code); SOURCE-TEXT-LEVEL-OBFUSCATION dimension distinct from all prior npm install-script/dependency cases because the payload is in the source TEXT itself using Unicode properties; defeats `diff` review and Unicode-normalizing scanners; GameZipper relevance: subagent game code committed without byte-level Unicode audit could ship homoglyph identifiers that look safe but resolve to malicious lookups (aikido.dev/blog/glassworm-returns-unicode-attack-github-npm-vscode Mar 13 2026)
- **S-125** [P1] PhantomRaven — npm Remote Dynamic Dependencies (RDD) hiding payload in an INVISIBLE runtime-fetched dependency so the reviewed package source is a clean "Hello world" stub (Oct 2025, 126 packages / 86K+ downloads); SPLIT-REVIEWED-VS-EXECUTED-CODE dimension distinct from S-105 (same-package lifecycle hook) and S-114 (provenance identity theft) because the reviewed code and executed code are physically different artifacts from different hosts; static source-review scanners all pass it; GameZipper mitigation: network-egress allowlist during npm install + --ignore-scripts + full transitive lockfile pinning (koi.ai/blog/phantomraven-npm-malware-hidden-in-invisible-dependencies Oct 29 2025)
- **S-126** [P1] eslint-config-prettier compromised via maintainer phishing — the npm account of JounQin (maintainer of eslint-config-prettier, 30M+ weekly downloads) was phished; attackers published malicious versions that executed arbitrary code on install (June 1 2026); PHISHING-OF-MAINTAINER dimension distinct from S-107 (bulk credential theft) and S-114 (stolen GitHub account) because this is direct social engineering of the human maintainer via spear-phish; the blast radius is every JS project that lints; GameZipper mitigation: exact-version + integrity-hash pinning, npm ci never npm install, --ignore-scripts for dev-only deps, advisory subscription (safedep.io/eslint-config-prettier-major-npm-supply-chain-hack June 1 2026)
- **S-127** [P1] AI chatbot recommendations redirect users to cryptojacking malware sites — attackers manipulate AI chatbots into RECOMMENDING cryptojacking/mining sites as legitimate resources (Cyber Post May 28 2026); AI-RECOMMENDATION-HIJACK dimension distinct from S-120 ChatGPhish (summarization injection) because the AI actively endorses the malicious site, lending it authority, far more clickable than a buried summary link; GameZipper angle: compromised game pages plant "recommended tool" hints the AI regurgitates to players querying about GameZipper games; mitigation: rel="nofollow sponsored" on outbound links, scan for cryptojacking resource hints, monitor AI responses mentioning GameZipper (thecyberpost.com May 28 2026)
- **W-157** [P2] AI chatbot news/game-summary >51% error rate distorting GameZipper game descriptions — BBC study (via sohu.com) found >51% of AI-generated summaries contain major errors (Gemini 46% worst, Copilot >50%, ChatGPT/Perplexity ~40%); applied to GameZipper: when a player asks an AI "what is this game?", over half the summaries misdescribe the game (wrong controls/objective/fabricated features); UNINTENTIONAL-HALLUCINATION dimension distinct from S-120/S-127 (malicious) but identical user-trust harm; mitigation: machine-readable JSON-LD VideoGame schema, concise canonical "How to play" as first readable text, periodic AI-summary audit (sohu.com BBC study; ejaw.net March 2026)
- **A-038** [P1] 2026 accessibility-lawsuit surge finals — 3,117 federal + 5,000 state-court website-accessibility lawsuits in 2025 (+27% YoY); DOJ extended ADA Title II to 2027/2028 for smaller entities; HHS Section 504 (health-program digital accessibility) hit May 11 2026 deadline — a NEW federal health-program mandate distinct from ADA Title II/III; distinct from A-034/A-035/A-036 because A-038 adds CONFIRMED 2025 FINAL NUMBERS (3,117 federal, not an estimate) + the HHS Section 504 health angle + the staggered 2027/2028 smaller-entity timeline; GameZipper mitigation: 3,117 as baseline risk, Section 504 self-assessment if any game has health claims (accessibility.build/research/accessibility-lawsuits; mantlr.com/blog/accessibility-lawsuit; accessible.org 2026 predictions)
- **C-106** [P2] Poki automated-playtesting integrated into developer SUBMISSION pipeline as a release gate (April 21 2026) — a game must PASS an automated playtest (canvas renders, level winnable, no fatal console error) before being accepted onto the platform; PLATFORM-INTEGRATED-PRE-RELEASE-QA-GATE distinct from C-075 (distribution surface), C-093 (enterprise tool), C-092 (method) because C-106 makes the playtest a HARD SUBMISSION BLOCKER not an optional step; GameZipper relevance: current pipeline relies on post-hoc QA (post-deploy-verification); Poki model is pre-registration gate that blocks games-data.js insertion on failure (roboticsandautomationnews.com/2026/04/21 April 21 2026; whimsygames.co May 5 2026)
- **G-145** [P2] 2026 mobile-game retention benchmarks — hyper-casual 48h-lapse threshold (helpshift.com 2026 re-engagement playbook) + 12% YoY UA-cost rise (gamegrowthadvisor.com March 17 2026); HYPER-CASUAL-LAPSE-ECONOMICS dimension distinct from G-143 (generic D1/D7/D30) because G-145 adds the hyper-casual-specific 48h lapse (re-engagement must fire at 48h not 7d) and the UA-cost-economics (every retained player worth 12% more); GameZipper mitigation: genre-aware 48h lapsed threshold, benchmark return-visit vs 38%/15% D1/D7, model 48h re-engagement window (helpshift.com; gamegrowthadvisor.com; ejaw.net March 2026)

## [v1.64.0] - 2026-06-16
### Added
- 8 new test cases from industry research (R184 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-120** [P1] ChatGPhish — AI-assistant web-summary feature abused to inject phishing URLs into AI-generated link summaries (June 2026) — AI-CONTENT-TRUST-LAYER abuse; users trust AI-summarized links more than raw URLs; an attacker who controls page content (malicious game page, poisoned leaderboard) embeds a hidden instruction causing a summarizing AI (ChatGPT browse, Gemini, Copilot, Apple Intelligence) to emit a phishing URL inside its prose summary; distinct from S-097 Chrome Gemini side-panel (browser surface) and S-101 extension prompt injection (needs execution) because S-120 needs no execution — just the AI including a link in its summary; GameZipper relevance: players ask AI assistants "what's this game?" → a compromised game page can poison every summarization (thehackernews.com June 2026 "ChatGPhish Vulnerability Turns ChatGPT Web Summaries Into a Phishing")
- **S-121** [P1] npm "Ghost campaign" (幽灵行动) — malicious npm packages print fake install logs (progress bars, hardcoded dependency names, randomized delays) to disguise credential-harvesting + RAT C2 deployment as a normal `npm install`; the deception defeats the #1 mitigation recommended for all prior npm cases ("watch the install output for anomalies") because even experienced developers cannot distinguish the fake output (Feb 2026 campaign, QQ News / Kaspersky March 27 2026); distinct from S-104 IndonesianFoods credential-theft and S-105 gyp bypass because the novelty is the DECEPTION-OF-DEVELOPER-CONSOLE technique; GameZipper relevance: subagent game builds run `npm install` — human/subagent eyeballing logs is defeated; mitigation: machine-parse ALL install output, network-egress allowlist to only registry.npmjs.org during install, `--ignore-scripts` by default
- **S-122** [P2] Dashlane password-manager offline brute-force on encrypted vaults (2026) — attackers brute-forced encrypted vaults of <20 users, demonstrating that even "zero-knowledge" vaults fall to offline brute-force when the master-password KDF is not strong enough; distinct from S-064 DBSC device-binding (protects live sessions, not exportable vault secrets) and prior PM-clickjacking cases (attack the fill UI, not the blob); mitigation: GameZipper must not recommend any single PM, use device-bound tokens not exportable vault secrets, document KDF assumption (Argon2id ≥64MB not PBKDF2-SHA1), rate-limit + lockout on auth surfaces, HIBP integration (thehackernews.com June 2026 "Dashlane Discloses Brute-Force Attack")
- **S-123** [P1] Fake browser-update phishing with clipboard / Win+R PowerShell self-typed execution flow (2026) — phishing pages mimicking Chrome security alerts now instruct victims to copy a payload to clipboard, press Win+R, Ctrl+V, Enter — running a PowerShell one-liner that fetches the real malware; defeats the dominant anti-phishing mitigation ("don't click links") because the victim TYPES the payload themselves (no clicked link for URL-filtering, no downloaded .exe for scanning); real-world example: javigd.com fake "Chrome Security Update Required" page observed June 14 2026 with exact "1 Press Win + R, 2 Press CTRL + V, 3 Press Enter" instructions; distinct from S-047 generic fake Chrome alert (covers the creative, not this delivery mechanism); GameZipper relevance: Monetag/AdSense ad slots could serve these creatives inside game pages — scan creatives for "Press Win + R" + clipboard-execution indicators, harden iframe sandbox (deny `clipboard-write`/`allow-top-navigation`), add `permissions-policy` denying `clipboard-write`
- **B-103** [P2] Basemark Web 3.0 → gpuscore.com benchmark-tool domain migration (redirects start 27.05.2026) — the flagship free browser-graphics benchmark moved domains; any GameZipper QA script or doc referencing `web.basemark.com` for GPU baselines hits a redirect (may break headless Playwright on `--headless=new`) and will eventually hit a dead page; TOOL-DEPENDENCY/STALE-URL dimension distinct from existing GPU-perf cases (P-035/P-037/P-046/P-047 test performance, not tooling deps); mitigation: grep test-library + scripts for `basemark`, update to `web.gpuscore.com`, add domain-liveness preflight to benchmark runners, re-capture any baselines captured on legacy URL (legacy scores not comparable to gpuscore.com scores) (web.basemark.com migration banner)
- **P-066** [P2] nierf.com community WebGPU/WebGL2 hashrate-style cross-device GPU leaderboard (June 2026) — new crowd-fed benchmark ranking GPU models + browsers by compute-throughput proxy; provides a CONTINUOUSLY-UPDATED device matrix that replaces the static P-048 entry-tier list (which rots as GPU landscape shifts quarterly); distinct from official Google WebAI Compute Benchmark C-097 (official but must be run per-device, expensive) because nierf.com is crowd-pre-run (free lookup); mitigation: adopt nierf.com p10/p50/p90 GPU as the canonical low/mid/high test devices, re-pull quarterly, cross-validate against on-device PerfDog measurements, monitor for leaderboard manipulation (nierf.com)
- **C-105** [P2] 2026 web-automation testing-platform selection guide requiring canvas-game smoke-test in POC (TestOne et al. June 11 2026) — web testing platforms bundle AI self-healing + stability scoring but vendor POC demos overwhelmingly use form/e-commerce pages; canvas-heavy game pages (GameZipper's entire catalog) expose a different failure surface (rAF timing, canvas pixel-diff, IIFE-encapsulated state) that form-page POCs never exercise; PLATFORM-PROCUREMENT dimension distinct from C-096/C-100/C-103 (self-healing feature critique, not vendor selection); mitigation: mandatory canvas-game smoke test in every POC (open canvas game, verify non-zero pixels, click + assert pixel change, screenshot baseline diff, drive to win/lose), reject platforms that only pass form demos, negotiate canvas-game SLA into contract (TestOne selection guide, so.html5.qq.com June 11 2026)
- **W-156** [P2] IndonesianFoods npm spam-flood reputational-pollution technique (Nov 2025, Kaspersky March 19 2026 deep-dive) — the campaign flooded npm with thousands of near-identical junk packages to (a) pollute npm search results so developers accidentally install typo-squatted spam packages and (b) degrade the signal-to-noise of security scanners (5,000 junk advisories bury the real high-severity one → alert fatigue); NOISE/REPUTATIONAL dimension distinct from S-104 credential-theft (the same campaign's other half — S-104 = what malicious packages DO once installed; W-156 = what spam packages do to the npm ECOSYSTEM INFRASTRUCTURE); mitigation: pin ALL deps never discover via npm search (pre-commit hook rejects unannotated new deps), scanner advisory de-duplication (collapse same-author/timestamp-cluster advisories), registry reputation scoring (block brand-new-account + generic-name packages), private npm mirror with explicit allowlist (Kaspersky "Spam packages in npm" March 19 2026)

### Sources
- Web search via minimax search (4 calls; web-search-prime batch timed out):
  - "Chrome Safari security vulnerability CVE June 2026" (minimax) — surfaced ChatGPhish, Gemini notification hijack context, DoubleClick DesckVB, Marimo, codexui-android, Dashlane, DBSC Chrome 146 GA, Ghost campaign (幽灵行动), IndonesianFoods Kaspersky deep-dive, fake-Chrome-update phishing page (javigd.com) with Win+R clipboard-execution instructions
  - "npm malicious package June 2026 supply chain attack" (minimax) — surfaced Ghost campaign (幽灵行动) fake-install-log RAT (so.html5.qq.com / QQ News March 27 2026), IndonesianFoods spam-flood (Kaspersky March 19 2026), npm supply-chain worm 2026 deep report (CSDN May 5 2026)
  - "ChatGPhish ChatGPT web summary phishing vulnerability 2026" (minimax) — confirmed ChatGPT/AI-summary-as-phishing-vector pattern (thehackernews.com wiretapping-label "This Week" digest June 2026)
  - "WebGPU browser performance benchmark mobile 2026 June" (minimax) — surfaced Basemark Web 3.0 → gpuscore.com migration (web.basemark.com banner, redirects start 27.05.2026), nierf.com Browser GPU Benchmark & Leaderboard (June 5 2026), TestOne web-automation platform selection guide (so.html5.qq.com June 11 2026)

## [v1.63.0] - 2026-06-16
### Added
- 8 new test cases from industry research (R183 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-116** [P1] OpenAI Codex CLI auth-token theft via `codexui-android` npm supply-chain attack (June 2026) — AI-CLI AUTH-TOKEN-compromise dimension targeting the long-lived API tokens Codex CLI stores in `~/.codex/auth.json` for CI/headless automation; distinct from S-101/S-106 Claude/Copilot browser-extension session cookies because CLI tokens are long-lived and billing-grade; sets the precedent that EVERY AI-coding-CLI's auth token is now a target (Gemini CLI, Cursor CLI, Aider, Continue.dev, Claude Code, Anthropic SDK tokens); GameZipper relevance: pipeline uses subagents via Claude Code, and if Codex CLI is ever added as ACP transport, `~/.codex/auth.json` becomes the crown jewel (thehackernews.com June 2026 "This Week OpenAI Codex Authentication Tokens Stolen in codexui-android npm Supply Chain Attack")
- **S-117** [P1] Gemini Android poisoned-notification hijack via WhatsApp / Slack / SMS / Signal / Instagram / Messenger (June 2026) — single poisoned notification can push victim into Zoom call, send a message disguised as user's boss, or quietly poison Gemini's long-term memory; extends Google's "Invitation Is All You Need" calendar-invite attack to the wider mobile-OS notification surface; distinct from S-097 Chrome Gemini Live side-panel CVE-2026-0628 because this targets the MOBILE-OS-NOTIFICATION surface not Chrome side panel; Google hardened Gemini against calendar-invite prompt injection but the notification channel remains exploitable; GameZipper angle: GameZipper game pages / walkthroughs / share-text become the VECTOR if a player's mobile AI assistant (Gemini, ChatGPT mobile, Copilot mobile, Apple Intelligence) ingests page content with embedded prompt-injection payloads (thehackernews.com June 2026 "WhatsApp, Slack Notifications Could Hijack Google Gemini on Android")
- **S-118** [P1] Google DoubleClick abused to deliver DesckVB RAT via malspam (June 3 2026) — legitimate Google-owned ad infrastructure abused; lure routes through DoubleClick before attacker-controlled infrastructure, evading ad-fraud detection that blocks known-bad domains (because first hop is Google's own `googleads.g.doubleclick.net`); paradigm shift for GameZipper which monetizes via AdSense + Monetag (both use DoubleClick) — a malicious creative that slips through DoubleClick's legitimate-looking chain lands directly in GameZipper game pages; distinct from S-054/S-058 AI-ad-fraud because this is LEGITIMATE-AD-PLATFORM-ABUSE-TO-DELIVER-RAT not IVT/fraud; distinct from B-050/B-073/B-102 Chrome CVEs because no browser bug is needed (the ad just runs JavaScript as designed) (thehackernews.com June 3 2026 "Google DoubleClick Abused in New Malspam Campaign to Deliver DesckVB RAT")
- **S-119** [P2] Marimo CVE-2026-39987 + LLM-agent post-exploitation pattern (June 2026) — attackers exploit Marimo then use the compromised LLM agent as the attacker's escalation / persistence / exfiltration channel via the agent's tool-call capabilities (file read, shell exec, web fetch); paradigm shift: prior AI-security tests (S-097/S-101/S-117) treated AI as the TARGET — S-119 documents the inverse pattern where AI is the ATTACKER'S TOOL after a non-AI compromise; GameZipper relevance: pipeline runs Hermes subagents with broad tool access (terminal + file + web + browser) — any other infra compromise (XSS, CI/CD token leak, misconfigured admin) can pivot to the Hermes agent and use its tools to escalate (read secrets, push malicious commits, exfiltrate the test library); mitigation: least-privilege toolsets, agent-tool-call allowlists, compartmentalized credentials (thehackernews.com June 2026 "Attackers Use LLM Agent for Post-Exploitation After Marimo CVE-2026-39987 Exploit")
- **C-103** [P2] Self-healing test-automation SILENT-false-pass detection — self-healing locators (Playwright Test Agents C-096, Browser Harness C-089, Codex CLI + Playwright MCP C-092) match a renamed-but-similar button and the test PASSES while masking real regression (action drift); for canvas-heavy games with volatile DOM this SILENT-WRONG-ELEMENT-MATCH is the dominant failure mode and is more dangerous than a normal test failure because no alarm fires; distinct from C-096 (introduces self-healing) and C-100 (critiques its hype) because C-103 provides the SPECIFIC DETECTION-MITIGATION methodology — semantic assertions layered on top of locator matches (expected state change + expected semantic label on top of click-target match) (qatechtools.com June 2 2026 + vericence.com + scrolltest.com)
- **C-104** [P2] Codex-CLI-as-QA-tool security constraint — when GameZipper QA uses Codex CLI as ACP transport (`kanban-codex-lane` skill pattern, or `delegate_task` with `acp_command: 'copilot'`), the codexui-android compromise risk (S-116) means Codex auth tokens in CI must be vault-rotated, least-privileged, and isolated; tooling-up QA must not introduce a NEW attack surface; operational-constraint dimension of S-116 — even without codexui-android installed, the broader pattern (AI-CLI auth tokens in CI) requires the same mitigations (vault rotation per-run, least-privilege token scope, sandboxed container with no prod-secret access, append-only audit log of every Codex invocation, instant-rotate kill-switch, canary-token detection, network-egress allowlist to only api.openai.com + github.com)
- **W-155** [P2] iOS 27 / iPadOS 27 / macOS Golden Gate WWDC26 stable-ship full-stack regression (June 9-13 2026 keynote → September 2026 public release) — Safari 27 stable ships, App Intents migration required for Siri 2.0 integration, Universal Links v3 (changed JSON schema), App Clips card UI changes, foldable-iPhone-ready iPad-style side-by-side multitasking; distinct from B-090/S-096 WWDC26 beta announcement because this is the POST-WWDC STABLE-SHIP milestone — features announced at WWDC sometimes get cut or changed before stable ship, the migration burden only becomes real at stable ship, and the iOS-27 install-base ramp (typically 50% within 6 weeks) determines when GameZipper must have full iOS 27 support (9to5mac.com June 12 2026 + macrumors.com + apple.com WWDC26)
- **A-037** [P1] iOS 27 Accessibility framework rewrite — VoiceOver notification-priority changes (announcements that were previously interruptive now queue differently), new Switch Control scanning patterns, rewritten Accessibility API for live regions; game canvas live regions must use updated APIs to announce score changes / level-complete events correctly to VoiceOver users; distinct from A-034/A-035/A-036 legal/methodology tests because this is a CONCRETE API-CHANGE regression test — iOS 27 changes how the Accessibility framework behaves at runtime and GameZipper code that worked on iOS 26 may silently break on iOS 27; distinct from B-090 Safari 27 WebKit fixes because A-037 covers the iOS-OS-level Accessibility framework (UIAccessibility, UIAccessibilityElement), not WebKit — even a perfect WebKit page can be inaccessible on iOS 27 if the OS-level Accessibility API usage is broken (apple.com WWDC26 + developer.apple.com accessibility sessions June 2026)

## [v1.62.0] - 2026-06-16
### Added
- 8 new test cases from industry research (R182 Dynamic Test Intelligence cron)
- **S-114** [P1] npm Sigstore provenance BYPASS via compromised maintainer account — 633 malicious npm package versions across 323 unique packages passed cryptographic provenance verification using valid Fulcio-issued signing certificates generated from a stolen GitHub maintainer account (May 19 2026, 48-hour window); defeats the "signed attestation = safe" assumption that S-105/S-107/S-109 mitigations rely on; the bypass was not a Sigstore protocol flaw but a maintainer-identity-trust flaw — a stolen GitHub account IS a valid GitHub Actions identity; distinct from S-111 TrapDoor cross-ecosystem coordination because this is the SIGNATURE-INFRASTRUCTURE-DEFEAT dimension (saassentinel.com May 23 2026 / ruberli.com May 22 2026 / venturebeat.com May 25 2026 / endorlabs.com / techbuddies.io / decryptiondigest.com)
- **S-115** [P2] Chrome 150 DevTools drawElementImage blank-canvas visual-regression-test bug — CDP Page.captureScreenshot / drawElementImage returns frozen/blank pixels for any WebGL/WebGPU/2D-canvas content that re-renders via requestAnimationFrame; breaks Playwright toHaveScreenshot / Percy / Chromatic / Applitools for canvas-heavy games; games render correctly on screen but CDP screenshots are blank → false-negative visual-regression tests; distinct from C-095 HTML-in-Canvas API introduction and C-098 WebGPU error handling because this is the TESTING-TOOL-DEPENDENCY dimension (github.com/WICG/html-in-canvas/issues/120 + issues.chromium.org/issues/522845799)
- **W-153** [P2] Chrome 150 (stable June 30 2026) is the FINAL Chrome version supporting macOS 12 Monterey; Chrome 151 (stable July 28 2026) requires macOS 13 Ventura — millions of older Intel/Apple-silicon Macs frozen on Chrome 150 indefinitely without security patches or new features; long-tail unsupported browser population; distinct from W-138/W-141 ChromeOS enterprise releases because this is CONSUMER macOS (9to5google.com / macrumors.com / support.google.com/chrome / forbes.com/zakdoffman / appleinsider.com / superchargebrowser.com Jan 2026)
- **W-154** [P2] Chrome 150.0.7869.0+ HTML-in-Canvas WebGL/WebGPU BREAKING API CHANGE per WICG working-group feedback — migration guide required for any code using drawElementImage() with WebGL/WebGPU target contexts; old API shape removed not deprecated; affects code adopted during the Chrome 149 origin-trial window (W-122, C-095); distinct from W-122/C-095 origin-trial introduction because this is the POST-STABLE BREAKING-API-CHANGE migration dimension (github.com/WICG/html-in-canvas/issues/132)
- **B-102** [P1] Chrome Android WebGL security regression pair — CVE-2026-9921 uninitialized-use cross-origin information disclosure + CVE-2026-9880 Critical-severity sandbox escape (both pre-148.0.7778.216); Android-specific (desktop Chrome WebGL NOT affected); exploit chain: malicious ad creative → CVE-2026-9921 renderer compromise reading GameZipper origin data → CVE-2026-9880 sandbox escape → device takeover; ~70% of GameZipper mobile traffic on Android bears full exposure; distinct from B-073/B-083 because this is ANDROID-PLATFORM + WEBGL-SPECIFIC (bugzilla.redhat.com/show_bug.cgi?id=2483084 + cvefeed.io/vuln/detail/CVE-2026-9880)
- **C-102** [P2] AI-discovered-CVE acceleration concrete QA-cadence impact — S-113 documented Mythos found 100 Chromium zero-days in 15 days; this C-102 test is the METHODOLOGY/CADENCE-RESPONSE: when Mythos-class tools drop 10+ Chromium CVEs in a day, the GameZipper test library must add regression tests within HOURS not the traditional week-long cycle; requires a rapid-CVE-response runbook + pre-built regression-test templates for common Chromium-bug patterns + cadence upgrade from 4h to 1h during active disclosure windows; distinct from S-113 discovery event because this is the PROCESS/PLAYBOOK dimension
- **A-036** [P1] Cognitive accessibility missing from self-managed audits — ADA Title II April 2026 deadline + 27% 2026 ADA-lawsuit surge + self-managed WCAG remediation systematically misses cognitive accessibility (instructions clarity / time-pressure relief / error recovery / complex-decision-flow documentation / working-memory load); automated scanners (axe/WAVE/Lighthouse) cover visual/motor/screen-reader but NOT cognitive; the 5 highest-impact ADA fixes per solid-web.com include cognitive-load reduction as the one self-managed audits miss; distinct from A-030/A-031 specific WCAG SCs and A-034/A-035 lawsuit surge because this is the COGNITIVE-DIMENSION + SELF-AUDIT-GAP angle (testparty.ai / solid-web.com / mantlr.com / levelaccess.com / wcagpros.com / webability.io)
- **G-144** [P2] Nordcurrent data-driven player drop-off per-level retention-curve analysis methodology — instrument per-level completion events + compute per-level retention curves + identify cliffs (levels with retention <80% of game median) + root-cause each cliff (difficulty spike / UX friction / tutorial gap / performance / monotony); Nordcurrent data shows first 5 levels account for ~60% of total drop-off; finds specific fixable friction points beyond aggregate D1/D7/D30 metrics; distinct from G-100/G-105 FTUE <3-tap and G-143 D1/D7/D30 benchmarks because this is the PER-LEVEL-GRANULARITY FRICTION-POINT-IDENTIFICATION methodology (80.lv Nordcurrent interview June 2026 / ejaw.net / gamegrowthadvisor.com)
